< Review>
Equipment is good, and they have a variety of stations to use. The only annoyance is the staff, who obviously don't use any type of lifting equipment in their life, come around interrupting your set of lifting to tell you how to use it properly and to move it. I'm sorry, are you telling me how to lift and what causes a hazard? When you actually have a healthy lifestyle of eating right and weightlifting experience, then you can interrupt my session to tell me I'm doing it wrong. Ive been lifting for 12years, dnt need them telling me how to and how not to lift. There's no reasoning with them. The little hawaiian/hispanic lady, not to be rude, started a fit about the placement of my equipment. It was NOT a hazard, but she was on my case about moving it, and gave the impression she was going to kick me out. I asked the guy staff that was there about the rules of equipment placement, they dnt have any. He showed me other placements, but those were more hazardous then where I had mine. I stated "theres no reasoning with yall, is there, just have to do it where you want huh?" And he said yes...<//Review>

< text>
Probably the worst gym I have been to in the Air Force. Granted I've only been to 8 AF gyms, but of the 8 this is the worst. Not enough machines/weights and the ones they do have are extremely close together making everything very crowded. The flow is very disorganized. I know I shouldn't complain, because it is free, but sometime free is not better. I know many people who pay out of pocket to go downtown so they avoid the on base gym.</text>

< review>
To summarize in a sentence; stay away from this surgeon if possible and only use as a last resort. Read below and decide for yourself.

- Very little medical knowledge, just surgical.

- If you have complications post-op, he'll send you off to various Doctors which offer no solutions.

- Takes on way too many patients causing very long wait times(1-2+ hrs).

- Takes a long time to get an appointment with him.

- His bariatric vitamins and shakes are expensive and you have to buy them or he won't do the surgery on you(it will cost about 300 dollars).

- The "dr. eslami" brand protein shake, are just the normal shakes with a label glued over. (I peeled the label off and saw the store brand label under it.)

- His bariatric vitamins are also overpriced but not too bad. You can find multi-vitamins online that have everything you need and the correct percentages if you mix and match. Don't do this if you are unsure.

-Afshin eslami is very cold, very uncaring about any of your problems and offers no solutions.(mostly because he doesn't know).

-Do not argue with him or he will delay your surgery as punishment. He delayed my surgery to the point where I was unsure if he was ever going to approve it.

- He'll use anything as an excuse to delay the surgery. For example, I was dieting and preparing for the surgery and made the mistake of saying I went out for fast food. Before I could say I had just a salad, he delayed my surgery and rushed me out of his office.

- Horrible bedside manner and a very poor understanding of medication and how it works.

- His lack of knowledge about gastrointestinal medication is shameful given his line of work. Go to your primary care or research online because he cannot help you regarding this matter.

- Day of surgery he will make you sign something saying that you can't sue him or take any action against him at all if he makes any mistakes or have any complications that arise from your stomach being too small. Standard except for that last part..

- Regarding the standard size of the gastric sleeve, he makes them smaller because it causes more compilations (i asked other bariatric surgeons about this). More complications means you are sicker for longer and lose more weight(this is the only plus). But you can have complications for longer then a year, like I did. I was forced to drop out of college because I was so sick I couldn't leave the house for the first 6 months.

-This Dr. Afshin Eslami really seems like he doesn't care at all about his patients, just about his stats and his wallet. He makes your sleeve small, you lose a ton of weight and then are stuck with the complications of losing weight too fast. You can't exercise too much because you are so nauseous all the time.

- All the medication you'll need to combat the complications may cost  500-2000 dollars a month(higher during the first 6 months) on medication and specialized food. You eat less but much more costly food to keep the complications at bay.

- Dr. eslami will tell you before surgery that he's never lost a patient, but after surgery he'll tell you that he's lost plenty; but never his fault.. One could think that this could be for your own good(lying to you to keep you scared like an adult does to a child), but all it does is cause a lack of trust between you and the surgeon. Not good when your life is in his hands.

- He's very self centered only caring about himself. For example he'll say things like, "I don't have to do this surgery, it's an elective surgery and I am not going to risk my career on you if you're just going to die"(sum) This is not the way a Doctor who's job is to help people, should act.

-If you have to use him, try and prepare for the complications that will come. Research online.

If you have to use Dr. eslami for bariatric surgeon, be very careful and expect complications after surgery. If you still have a choice in surgeon, choose a better one. I hope any of this information will or has helped you. Choose your surgeon very carefully or it could cost you your life, livelihood or both.< /review>

Discovered this place literally by accident. While making a left onto 5th street from Brush St. heading towards Jack London Square, I happened to see their sandwich board sign on the corner of 5th and Brush. It was really random. Anyhow, the first time I saw their signage, was on a saturday and they closed early, so I made sure the next time I was in the area, I would stop by.

This bakery is located in a building that looks like a gingerbread house from the outside, it's really cute. The trim is painted with fun colors.

The bakery is small inside. When you enter, there is a small sitting room to the left hand side, and a display of the cupcakes on white pedestals in a display case in front of you.

The cupcakes can also be gluten free or vegan. There are signs next to the cupcake pedestals that list the ingredients. The cupcakes are $3 each.

I ended up buying 3 cupcakes, 1 is gluten free. I haven't had the chance to try them yet, but am looking forward to consuming them.

Parking is free and it's all street parking.</review>

< review>
This place is unique, friendly, and has some very interesting taste combinations. I enjoyed the cupcake flavor combination that that I purchased however I was a little disappointed with how easily it fell apart as I ate. It was a very very moist cupcake. Almost too moist as it fell apart into mush. The cake pops were also too soft / mushy I took one bite into my cake pop and it fell right off the stick into the dirt I was very disappointed. It is also a bit pricey for cupcakes but I suppose that is due to there unique cupcake creations. Also one of the kids I got cupcakes with purchased a vegan mint chocolate chip cupcake. She did not like it probably because it was vegan and she was not use to the lack of animal probucts. She ended up giving it to her mother who also did not like it. On the upside of my experience everything I tasted did taste unique and delicious. The server/cashier was very patient and friendly she provided great customer service. I also noticed that they did have several vegan and gluten-free options for people who have gluten intolerance or food preferences.< /review>

< review>
I visited this Chipotle last night while I was in Vallejo (I live in San Jose) and I cannot express my experience more positively. When I showed up I was surprised to find that you could not order inside due to to Covid (the restrictions apparently haven‚Äôt been lifted in Solano County like they have been in Santa Clara County) but that isn‚Äôt Chipotle‚Äôs fault of course.

I downloaded the app on the spot and ordered two burritos and a large chips and guac. The food was ready in less than 10 minutes despite there being a lot of mobile orders sitting on the table inside the restaurant.

When I actually went to eat the burrito I was extremely impressed with the presentation of the food. My burrito was quite large (I ordered chicken and carnitas, with everything else on it besides guac and queso) and the burrito was tightly and expertly wrapped. I worked at Chipotle back in 2018-2019 and I know firsthand how much skill it takes to wrap a burrito with that much stuff on it, especially when it gets watered down with all the salsa and sour cream. I ate the burrito in my car and it didn‚Äôt drip or fall apart at all.

That‚Äôs not to mention the taste of the burrito, either; this was quite possibly the best Chipotle burrito I‚Äôve ever had, despite me having made MANY burritos myself to my own liking during my time working there. It was extremely good, and the chips were made to perfection as well. My only gripe was that the number of chips was a bit low, but I‚Äôll let it slide since we admittedly did visit a bit late and I know from my time working there that the number of chips tend to dwindle the later it gets. Still though, for a large bag of chips I feel like we should have gotten more.

Still 5 stars for this great experience, though. Keep up the great work!<//review>
